## Findings

| ID | Chunk | Severity | Category | Status | File | Function / Area | Summary | Why it matters | Suggested direction | Evidence |
|----|-------|----------|----------|--------|------|-----------------|---------|----------------|---------------------|----------|
| AUD-0001 | 1 | Critical | Bug | Resolved | lib/tradelens/core/pg_pool.py | `get_db_connection` context manager | Replaced the `try/except InterfaceError / else` shape with `try/except InterfaceError / finally` + a `close_it` flag. `pool.putconn(conn, close=close_it)` now runs on every exit path, so non-InterfaceError exceptions no longer leak the connection. | — | — | Fixed 2026-04-23. Regression tests: test_pg_pool.py::TestGetDbConnectionLifecycleAUD0001 (3 — non-InterfaceError path, InterfaceError path, clean exit). |
| AUD-0002 | 1 | Critical | Reliability | Resolved | lib/tradelens/adapters/bybit_client.py | `_request` (and all order/read methods) | No retry, backoff, rate-limit, or circuit-breaker handling on the sole exchange client. **Design 2026-04-26 (cluster commit `44871bdf` paired with AUD-0008):** comprehensive 4-phase design at `docs/30-fixes-and-audits/audits/audit-autofix/2026-04-26-aud-0002-0008-convergence-design.md` (507 lines). **Phase A-1 shipped 2026-04-30 (this commit):** GET-only retry loop in `_request` with exponential backoff (1s → 2s, 3 attempts max) gated by `$TRADELENS_BYBIT_RETRY_ENABLED` env-flag (off by default — operators flip on per-host once smoke validates). Retries on 429, 5xx (500/502/503/504), and network exceptions (`httpx.TimeoutException`, `httpx.NetworkError`, `httpx.ConnectError`, `httpx.ReadError`, `httpx.RemoteProtocolError`). Each attempt re-signs the request (recv_window=5s otherwise stales). One structured WARNING `bybit.retry endpoint=… attempt=… cause=… sleep_s=…` log per retry — retries can't mask transient bugs because retry rate is observable. POSTs single-attempt (A-3 will add idempotent POST retries guarded by orderLinkId presence). retCode!=0 (application errors like "insufficient balance") never retried. **Phase A-2 shipped 2026-04-30 (this commit):** rate-limit headers (`X-Bapi-Limit`, `X-Bapi-Limit-Status`, `X-Bapi-Limit-Reset-Timestamp`) parsed from every response (and 429s) and stored in per-endpoint sliding-window state on the BybitClient instance under `self._rate_limit_lock`. On 429 retry the adapter now honours the response's reset-timestamp (clamped to `RATE_LIMIT_SLEEP_CAP_SECONDS`=4s) instead of the static A-1 backoff. Pre-emptive throttle: when last-observed `remaining/limit < PRE_THROTTLE_FRACTION`=0.1, the next call sleeps until reset_ms before firing — cheap path that prevents 429 in the first place. Per-endpoint state isolation (hot `/v5/order/*` does not throttle `/v5/market/*`). Structured `bybit.rate_limit_throttle endpoint=… remaining_pct=… sleep_s=…` WARNING per pre-throttle. Same `$TRADELENS_BYBIT_RETRY_ENABLED` env-flag gates A-2 (additive when off). **Phase A-3 shipped 2026-04-30 (this commit):** POST retry guarded by orderLinkId presence. New `_post_is_retryable(params)` helper splits POSTs: orderLinkId-keyed (`place_order` always-on via AUD-0039, `cancel_by_order_link_id`, `place_conditional_order` per AUD-0039 b, optional `amend_order` per AUD-0039 b) → retry like GETs. orderId-keyed (`cancel_order`, `amend_order` without olid, `set_trading_stop`, `set_leverage`, `clear_position_take_profit`) → NEVER retry (Bybit cancel/amend is idempotent on orderId so the conservative single-attempt is documented in design A.3.1). Retry sends the SAME orderLinkId each attempt so Bybit's dedupe is the safety net. Empty/None/whitespace orderLinkId treated as "absent" (defensive). retCode!=0 still never retried. **Phase A-4 shipped 2026-04-30 (this commit):** per-endpoint circuit breaker. Three-state machine (closed/open/half_open) with `CIRCUIT_BREAKER_THRESHOLD`=0.5 strict (>50% failure rate), `CIRCUIT_BREAKER_WINDOW_SECONDS`=60, `CIRCUIT_BREAKER_MIN_REQUESTS`=5 (don't open on 1-of-1 noise), `CIRCUIT_BREAKER_COOLDOWN_SECONDS`=30 initial, doubles on canary failure capped at `CIRCUIT_BREAKER_COOLDOWN_MAX_SECONDS`=300 (5 min). State stored on the BybitClient instance under `self._circuit_breaker_lock`. Behind `$TRADELENS_BYBIT_CIRCUIT_BREAKER_ENABLED` env-flag (off by default — design A.5 risk #3 says ship dark, soak the existing retry-rate logs first to validate the threshold isn't going to fire on routine Bybit hiccups). When OPEN: raises `ExchangeError("circuit open: …")` BEFORE any network call. After cooldown: next call is the canary; success → CLOSED + cooldown reset; failure → re-OPEN with doubled cooldown. retCode!=0 (application errors) explicitly NOT counted toward the breaker. Per-endpoint isolation. Structured `bybit.circuit_open endpoint=… cooldown_total_s=… reason=…` and `bybit.circuit_close endpoint=… reason=canary_succeeded` WARNINGS. Per-endpoint rate-limit budget chosen (matches Bybit's quota structure). **Scope note (2026-04-30, post-flip soak):** AUD-0002 retry/throttle/breaker only wraps `bybit_client._request`. The mdsync candle fetcher (`lib/tradelens/mdsync/fetcher.py`) opens its own `httpx.Client` and bypasses this code path — verified empirically when the retry flag was flipped on rocky2 mdsync_pg and produced 0 retry events despite 14× "Too many visits" rate-limit hits at the 14:00 UTC minute boundary. The flag was rolled back on rocky2 (kept on rocky-8gb api). mdsync has its own AUD-0274 shared RPS limiter (5 RPS on rocky-8gb where the IP is shared, 20 RPS on rocky2 where it has a dedicated IP) and tolerates rate-limit errors at the application level (next cycle re-fetches). If AUD-0002 protections turn out to be needed in mdsync, follow-up audit required (options: route mdsync through `bybit_client` OR port the retry/throttle logic into `mdsync/fetcher.py`). Risks documented: retries can mask | Any 429/5xx surfaces as immediate failure; pipeline bursts can trip bans; POSTs without orderLinkId can't be safely retried anywhere upstream. | Add retry policy for GETs and for POSTs with orderLinkId only; honour `X-Bapi-Limit-Reset-Timestamp`; add circuit breaker. | Grep: 0 hits for `retry\|backoff\|rate.limit\|429\|sleep` in bybit_client.py. |

| AUD-0008 | 1 | Major | Architecture | Resolved | lib/tradelens/core/ (pg_pool, pg_db, db_pool) | `PooledDB`, `PostgresDB`, `get_db_connection`, shim | Three overlapping DB-access patterns; API mostly uses the manual-close variant. **Design 2026-04-26 (cluster commit `44871bdf` paired with AUD-0002):** convergence design within the same 507-line doc. Canonical pattern: `with get_db_connection() as conn: ...` for FastAPI (existing context manager). `PostgresDB` for standalone scripts kept (has AUD-0184 test seam — must NOT delete). Delete `PooledDB` + `db_pool.py` 29-line back-compat shim. Phased migration: B-1 audit usage; B-2..B-5 migrate API in batches of ~5 files (~25 PooledDB-using files identified); B-6 services/ dual-context callers (`push_sender.py`, `pushover_sender.py`, `ai_snapshot.py`) need per-file decision; B-7 delete shim once all imports migrated. Verified counts: 25 unique files import `PooledDB` (181 line-occurrences); 30 files import via `db_pool` shim (union of PooledDB-importers + 7 get_db_connection-via-shim). 20 of 25 PooledDB files are in `lib/tradelens/api/`. Risks: context-manager scope changes lifetime semantics; some code may rely on long-lived state (services/ flagged). **B-2 shipped 2026-04-30:** templates.py (5 sites), alerts.py (8 sites), push.py (3 sites), screenshots.py (2 sites) — 18 PooledDB sites converted. Used a tokenize-aware migration script to skip multi-line string interiors (avoided corrupting an HTML f-string in `_render_screenshot_view`). **B-3 shipped 2026-04-30:** correlation.py (1 site), vwap.py (8 sites), vwap_orders.py (5 sites), order_sets.py (4 sites), suspend.py (7 sites) — 25 more PooledDB sites converted. Migration script extended to handle: Pattern A blank-lines between `db = PooledDB` and `try:`; Pattern P with `db = None` outside try + `if db: db.close()` finally guard; mixed finally blocks with other cleanups (`if bybit:` / `if lock:`) — surgical removal of just the db-cleanup lines. Dropped now-dead `config = get_config()` lines and matching imports. Updated `tests/integration/test_aud0218_suspend_intra_lock_transaction.py` to patch `get_db_connection` (returning a context manager) instead of `PooledDB`. (The B-3 migration files were swept into commit `0992a6f0` by a concurrent session with a misleading `feat(breach-decision)` message — work is correct, history is just suboptimal.) **B-4 shipped 2026-04-30:** notes.py (6 sites), journal.py (18 sites — biggest at 5312 LOC, uses `atomic_block` transaction wrapper), guards.py (5 sites), spot.py (1 site), trade_alerts.py (6 sites — wasn't in the design doc's batch boundaries, included to keep the file count moving). Per-axis values replace the pre-fix 30s scalar; a hung TCP handshake now fast-fails in 5s instead of holding a worker thread for half a minute. `httpx.Limits` and `HTTPTransport(retries=2)` are deferred — option (a) ships only the timeout change to keep the blast radius small. | — | — | Fixed 2026-04-26. | AUD-0012 | 1 | Major | Reliability | Resolved | lib/tradelens/core/account_context.py | `AccountContext.__init__` | Lazy DB reload on the first ``get_account_id()`` cache miss when the initial DB load failed; ``_db_load_succeeded`` flag gates exactly one retry per miss to avoid hammering the DB while it's down. Once a load has succeeded, the cache is trusted for the rest of the process; ``reload()`` resets the flag for explicit invalidation. A recovered DB now heals the cache on the next lookup — no process restart required. | — | — | Fixed 2026-04-27. Commit: `98397fb7`. Regression test: tests/unit/test_aud0012_0037_0016_0038_core_cluster.py (covers lazy reload after failed initial load, no retry after success, exactly-one-retry-per-miss when DB stays down, reload-resets-flag). | AUD-0013 | 1 | Major | Reliability | Resolved | lib/tradelens/core/pg_pool.py | `get_db_connection` and `PooledDB.close` | Both `putconn` paths now emit a WARNING log (`logger.warning("putconn failed …")`) instead of `except Exception: pass`. Failures are still swallowed — a shutdown-race putconn shouldn't crash the handler — but they now leave a trail so "pool exhausted with no logs" stops being a silent class of incident. `PooledDB.close` applies the same treatment to the direct-connection close path for symmetry. | — | — | Fixed 2026-04-23. | AUD-0016 | 1 | Major | Config | Resolved | lib/tradelens/core/config.py | `AppConfig` | Each known nested section (database, postgresql, trading, risk, ui, screenshots, vwap, timeframes, suspend) is now parsed through a strict (`extra='forbid'`) typed Pydantic schema in AppConfig's `model_validator(mode='after')`. A typo in config.yml (e.g. ``hsot:`` for ``host:``) raises ValidationError at AppConfig construction → app fails fast at startup. AppConfig field types stay `Optional[Dict[str, Any]]` so the 30+ existing call sites reading ``config.database['host']``-style don't change. Adding a new key requires updating the schema (the explicit fail-fast surface the audit asked for). | — | — | Fixed 2026-04-27. Commit: `98397fb7`. | AUD-0017 | 1 | Minor | Suspicious | Resolved | lib/tradelens/main.py | `periodic_gc` | Loop deleted along with `_gc_stats`, `import gc`, the `gc_task = asyncio.create_task(...)` startup line, and the matching `gc_task.cancel()` shutdown block. Lifespan now starts up DB pool + candle reader + thread executor, yields, then cleans up Bybit clients + executor + candle reader + DB pool. | — | — | Fixed 2026-04-25. Verified cargo-cult by 2026-04-25 read-only investigation: loop was added belt-and-braces in commit 5d4ca00b (2025-12-16) alongside the actual OOM fix (DB connection pooling). Pooling solved the leak; the GC loop has been running on autopilot for 4+ months (180,000+ runs) with API RSS steady at ~90 MB and generational counts flat — no underlying retention to justify it. All real retention sources (executor, bybit_client, pools) are explicitly cleaned in lifespan shutdown. No regression test (dead-code removal is exempt per test policy). | AUD-0039 | 1 | Major | Architecture | Resolved | lib/tradelens/adapters/bybit_client.py | Order placement | No idempotency convention: `order_link_id` optional, no generation helper, no cancel-by-link-id. **Resolved 2026-04-26 (option a): adapter boundary now auto-populates orderLinkId.** Module-level constant `ORDER_LINK_ID_MAX_LEN=36` + helpers `_generate_order_link_id(trade_id, leg_kind)` and `_validate_order_link_id(value)`. `place_order` enforces the policy: caller-supplied values are validated (non-empty + ≤36 chars) and passed through; missing values are generated as `{trade_id}-{leg_kind}-{ts_ms}{jitter6}` (jitter is `secrets.token_hex(3)`, ~24 bits — eliminates intra-millisecond collisions for rapid back-to-back recovery / multi-leg setup; format spirit preserved). When trade_id or leg_kind is missing the corresponding component falls back to `secrets.token_hex(4)`. Truncation preserves the trailing timestamp+jitter suffix when prefix is oversized. New method `cancel_by_order_link_id(symbol, category, order_link_id)` mirrors `cancel_order` but cancels via Bybit's `orderLinkId`. No caller sweep — every existing `order_link_id=None` site now gets auto-populated at the boundary. Prerequisite to safe POST retries (AUD-0002); unblocks Bucket C Tier 3 items AUD-0231 (resume recreate) and AUD-0282 (vwap amend). Regression tests: tests/unit/test_aud0039_orderlinkid_adapter.py (10 — generator length cap with both/missing args, truncates oversized prefix, unique under rapid calls; place_order auto-generate / pass-through / rejects empty / rejects oversized; cancel_by_order_link_id payload + input validation). Targeted sweep `pytest tests/unit/ -k "bybit or order_link or adapter"`: 47 passed. Commit `1a388ff5` (cherry-picked with additive merge against AUD-0027/AUD-0015/AUD-0086 module constants). **Update 2026-04-26 (option b — commit `d9e36e15`):** extended the same orderLinkId policy to the two remaining money-moving adapter methods that (a) left out: `amend_order(..., order_link_id=None)` and `place_conditional_order(..., order_link_id=None, trade_id=None, leg_kind=None)`. `amend_order` is identification-only — caller-supplied + validated + included in payload alongside `orderId` for retry safety; default-None preserves all legacy callers (no auto-generation since amend targets an existing order). `place_conditional_order` mirrors `place_order` exactly: caller-supplied is validated and passed through; None triggers `_generate_order_link_id`. AUD-0039 (a) helpers (`_generate_order_link_id`, `_validate_order_link_id`) byte-for-byte unchanged; lock-in test `test_aud0039_generator_and_validator_unchanged` in the new test file pins this. Unblocks AUD-0282 (vwap_order_engine.amend_order migration), AUD-0231's parked conditional branch, AUD-0114/0115 typed-routing migration, AUD-0002 future POST retry policy at both endpoints. No caller migration in this commit. Regression tests: tests/unit/test_aud0039b_amend_conditional_order_link_id.py (8). Combined regression sweep with AUD-0039 (a) tests: 18 passed. **Update 2026-04-27 (env-hook follow-up — commit `90b8bdf2`):** added `TRADELENS_AUD0272_PROFILE` env-var override branch in `_load_runner_tuning` so an operator can flip `profile_aud0272` without editing tracked `etc/config.yml`. Accepts `1/true/yes/on` → True, `0/false/no/off` → False; any other value (or absence) falls through to YAML setting. Mirrors the env-override pattern in `lib/tradelens/core/config.py`. AUD-0272 bool-only YAML validation preserved unchanged. Closes the operational gap noted in the AUD-0272 step E soak operator note (commit `2c540d0d`). Regression tests: tests/unit/test_aud0039b_env_var_profile_override.py (8 functions, 23 cases via parametrize). | Prerequisite to safe POST retries (AUD-0002); dedupe on read also weak. | Auto-generate orderLinkId per order; require it; add `cancel_by_order_link_id`. | bybit_client.py:698-745, 962-985. |

| AUD-0078 | 3 | Critical | Performance | Resolved | lib/tradelens/api/open_orders.py | `refresh_order_data` | Every mutation spawned `python3 refresh_order_leg_live.py` as a subprocess and blocked the API worker up to 10–15s on every cancel / amend / convert / create. **Resolved 2026-04-26 (option b — BackgroundTasks):** moved the post-mutation refresh into FastAPI `BackgroundTasks` at the four call sites where the response does NOT depend on the refresh having run: `cancel_order` (line 824), `amend_order` convert-to-LevelGuard branch (line 1614), `amend_order` guard-disable branch (line 1907), and `amend_order` regular non-guarded branch (line 2312). Each handler now declares `background_tasks: BackgroundTasks = None` (default `None` keeps internal Python callers and direct-call test fixtures working — FastAPI auto-injects on real HTTP requests) and uses `background_tasks.add_task(refresh_order_data, ...)` as the primary path. Two call sites were INTENTIONALLY left synchronous because the response immediately reads / updates the row that `refresh_order_data` is responsible for inserting: `convert_to_limit` (line 2927 → followed by `UPDATE order_leg_live SET lineage_id WHERE exchange_order_id = new`) and `create_order` (line 4203 → followed by `SELECT id FROM order_leg_live WHERE exchange_order_id = new` and the leg_type / VWAP-linkage chain). **Update 2026-04-26 (option B follow-up — commit `31a5caf7`):** the two formerly-synchronous sites now use Option B — inline INSERT into `order_leg_live` from the Bybit response payload + request inputs (with `ON CONFLICT (exchange_order_id) DO NOTHING` for safe concurrent-BG-arrival), then run the dependent lineage UPDATE / SELECT-id / VWAP-linkage chain synchronously, then schedule the full `refresh_order_data(...)` as a `background_tasks.add_task(...)`. Both handlers gained `background_tasks: BackgroundTasks = None` with sync-fallback when None (internal Python callers). Response shape unchanged. The minimal inline-INSERT populates only NOT-NULL columns verifiable from the create-order response + request inputs (`account_id`, `symbol`, `action`, `exchange_order_id`, `leg_type` placeholder from `determine_leg_type()` or source row, `order_kind`, `qty`, `status`, `category`, `updated_at`); the BG full refresh re-classifies and overwrites via `refresh_order_leg_live.py`'s `if old_snapshot:` UPDATE branch — no double-INSERT under `UNIQUE(exchange_order_id)`. The `# AUD-0078: this call site is INTENTIONALLY synchronous` markers were removed and replaced with brief `# AUD-0078 (option B): inline-INSERT minimal row, sync lineage UPDATE, then BG full refresh` comments. | AUD-0081 | 3 | Critical | Reliability | Resolved | lib/tradelens/api/open_orders.py | cancel / convert-to-limit / create / amend | All four mutation endpoints now wrap their bodies in `AppLock(namespace='order-mutation', ttl_seconds=30, wait_seconds=2)` via the thin-wrapper-then-`_<endpoint>_locked`-helper pattern. lock_key choices: `cancel_order` / `convert_to_limit` / `amend_order` use per-leg `f'leg-{request.order_id}'` (any cross-mutation race on the same leg fast-fails with 409); `create_order` has no pre-existing leg_id and uses `f'create-trade-{request.trade_id}-{request.order_type}-{request.order_kind}'` (prevents same-button double-click duplicates while allowing concurrent multi-leg setup like entry+SL+TP fired close together — different (order_type, order_kind) tuples → different keys → no collision). role tags: 'cancel', 'convert-to-limit', 'amend', 'create' for observability. amend_order's pre-existing inner AppLock at ~1991 (former role='guard-disable', wait_seconds=5) used the same lock_key as the new outer wrap and was replaced with `contextlib.nullcontext()` to preserve the ~600-line disable-LG indented body without rewrite — leaving it would have deadlocked (PostgreSQL PK conflict on same key acquired twice). The re-read-under-lock pattern below the former inner lock remains as a cheap defensive extra DB read (semantically redundant once the outer lock is held but harmless). On contention all four endpoints raise `HTTPException(409, "...is currently being modified by another request — please retry")`. `bulk_cancel_orders` continues calling `cancel_order(_defer_refresh=True)` and acquires per-order locks for each delegation; per-order failures surface as per-order results so a stuck lock on one leg in a bulk doesn't fail the whole batch. | — | — | Fixed 2026-04-28 (Campaign 2 Day 1 Wave A continuation across two commits: `829f2405` cancel + convert; `ac17e4df` amend + create + Wave A close). Regression tests: tests/unit/test_aud0081_applock_mutations.py (16 cases — wrap source-shape per endpoint, namespace + per-leg/per-(trade,type,kind) lock_key per endpoint, role tag per endpoint, 409 translation per endpoint, helper-body sanity guards per endpoint, inner-AppLock-replaced-with-nullcontext check on `_amend_order_locked`, wait_seconds=2 / ttl_seconds=30 invariants across all four wrappers, lock_key composition check for create_order). | AUD-0094 | 3 | Major | Bug | Resolved | lib/tradelens/api/open_orders.py | `preview_amend_order` vs `preview_order` | `position_after` calculation diverges; qty=0 handling differs. **Resolved 2026-04-26 (option a — ported `preview_amend_order` to `preview_order` shape, inline rather than via shared helper):** `preview_amend_order` and `preview_order` in `lib/tradelens/api/open_orders.py` produced divergent UI output for equivalent inputs because they classified close orders with two different leg-type lists and handled the Bybit reduce-only `qty=0` "entire position" sentinel differently. Specifically: (1) `preview_amend_order` had two parallel lists — `is_close_order_check` (line 1046, included `'sl'`) gated the qty=0 → position-size substitution, while `is_close_order` (line 1073, omitted `'sl'`) gated the P&L branch — so an `'sl'` leg got the qty substitution but produced no P&L estimate; (2) `preview_amend_order` overwrote `effective_qty` with `position_size` when the user submitted qty=0 on a close order, then returned `calculated_qty=str(effective_qty)` (e.g. `'10.0'`), so the frontend's check `calculated_qty !== '0' ? <number> : 'Entire'` (`frontend/web/src/components/shared/order-preview-display.tsx:55`) rendered the numeric qty instead of the `'Entire'` label that `preview_order`'s `'0'` sentinel correctly triggered. (3) `position_after` for amend computed via subtraction in all cases, while `preview_order` short-circuited to `'0'` for the entire-close path (`open_orders.py:3585-3592`), creating subtle string-form differences (`'0.0'` vs `'0'`) even when the float values agreed. Fix: introduced a single `is_close_order` list (matching `preview_order`'s classification, including `'sl'`) used by both the qty-sentinel branch and the P&L branch; introduced `qty_for_calc` mirroring `preview_order`'s `qty_float` so the entire-close case uses position_size for P&L while leaving `effective_qty` at 0 for the response; rendered `calculated_qty` (and `bybit_params['qty']`) as the bare `'0'` sentinel when `is_entire_close`, matching `preview_order` exactly; matched the position_after short-circuit (`if is_entire_close: position_after = '0'`). Shape A (inline port) chosen over Shape B (shared helper) because the divergent block is ~10 lines while the surrounding code differs significantly between the two functions (validation, request shape, VWAP resolution, leg_type derivation) — extracting a helper would have required ~15 parameters and added more code than it removed. Function signatures and `PreviewOrderResponse` shape unchanged; only the divergent value computation moved. FE-shape contract verified preserved: every field the FE consumes (`PreviewOrderResponse` TS interface in `frontend/web/src/lib/api.ts:1569`) is still present with the same types. Regression test: `tests/integration/test_aud0094_preview_unification.py` (5 cases — qty=0 entire-close sentinel, create-vs-amend parity for partial close, FE-shape preservation, zero-position edge case, open-order DCA path). Pre-fix the qty=0 entire-close test would assert `body['calculated_qty'] == '0'` and fail with `'0.0' != '0'`; post-fix it passes. | AUD-0101 | 3 | Minor | Bug | Resolved | lib/tradelens/api/open_orders.py | `_price_decimals` | Uses `f"{price:.10f}".rstrip('0')` on floats. **Resolved 2026-04-26 (this commit, bundled with AUD-0103):** replaced the `f"{price:.10f}".rstrip('0')` printf-trick with `Decimal(str(price)).normalize().as_tuple().exponent`, matching the Decimal-everywhere pattern this file already follows for `round_to_tick` / `round_qty_to_step`. The old approach under-counted scientific-notation floats outside the format's 10-digit precision range (e.g. `1e-12` formatted to `"0.0000000000"`, rstripped to `"0."`, returned 0 instead of 12) and could over-count Decimals with declared trailing zeros (e.g. a `numeric(38,10)` column arriving as `Decimal("0.0500000000")`). The new implementation accepts `float`, `int`, `Decimal`, or numeric-string inputs and reports the count of significant decimal places. Function signature relaxed from `float` to untyped (callers — both still pass the same `trade['waep']` float — see open_orders.py:1093 and :3506); zero-special-case (`return 2`) preserved. Regression test: `tests/unit/test_aud0101_0103_decimal_compare.py` (10 cases for this row including the `1e-12` regression and the `Decimal("1.50000")` trailing-zero case). | Scientific-notation floats over-report decimals. | Decimal-based inspection. | open_orders.py:2134-2141. |

| AUD-0106 | 3 | Minor | Reliability | Resolved | lib/tradelens/api/open_orders.py | `get_qty_step` / `get_tick_size` fallbacks | Silent fallback to `Decimal('0.0001')` / `Decimal('0.01')`. **Resolved 2026-04-26 (option a — raise on unknown):** both helpers in `lib/tradelens/api/open_orders.py` (`get_qty_step` at line 3264 and `get_tick_size` at line 3315 — note line drift from the audit's 2890/2950-2956) now raise `fastapi.HTTPException(status_code=400, detail="Unknown instrument: <symbol> (<category>). qty_step/tick_size is not available.")` instead of silently returning a wrong-precision Decimal. The HTTPException type was chosen over `ValueError` because every caller of these helpers is already inside a FastAPI handler that follows the `except HTTPException: raise; except Exception as e: raise _sanitize_internal_error(...)` pattern (verified: preview_amend_order, amend_order, convert_to_limit, preview_order, create_order in open_orders.py; amend_order_set in order_sets.py — 13+ existing `HTTPException(400)` raises in the same file confirm the convention). Raising any other exception type would be re-wrapped by `_sanitize_internal_error` to a generic HTTP 500, hiding the actual cause from the user. Non-FastAPI caller `bin/server/level_guard_daemon.py` (lines 573, 639, 641) wraps in `except Exception` → `_classify_execution_exception(e)` → falls through to `EXEC_AMBIGUOUS` for unknown exception types, so HTTPException propagates correctly there too. Inside `get_tick_size` the bare `except Exception` was tightened to re-raise as HTTPException(400) instead of swallowing the error and falling through to the fallback; an explicit `except HTTPException: raise` re-raise was added so the explicit unknown-instrument error doesn't get caught and re-wrapped by the bare exception handler. The secondary `or '0.0001'` fallback in `get_qty_step`'s lookup chain (`lot_filter.get('qtyStep') or lot_filter.get('basePrecision') or '0.0001'`) was also removed and replaced with an `if not qty_step: raise` guard. Caller-count: 8 call-site groups, all already wrapping exceptions correctly — zero new try/except blocks needed (stop condition not triggered). Regression test: `tests/unit/test_aud0106_raise_on_unknown_instrument.py` (10 cases — 4 for each helper + 2 contract tests pinning the exception type to `fastapi.HTTPException` with `status_code=400` so callers can rely on the contract). | AUD-0118 | 4 | Major | Reliability | Resolved | lib/tradelens/api/trades.py + journal.py + batch_ideas.py + notes.py | no COMMIT / ROLLBACK in 9,189 lines | Every multi-row/multi-table write runs on autocommit. | Any mid-stream failure leaves partial state; reinforces existing SPLIT-BRAIN log. | Explicit transactions on mutations; autocommit for reads only. | grep COMMIT/ROLLBACK → 0 hits. **2026-04-25 (cluster sweep): partial-stop**. The "ideas-overwrite" sub-path called out in `decisions-pending.md` does not actually live in `lib/tradelens/api/journal.py` — the real ideas-overwrite multi-table writer is at `lib/tradelens/api/batch_ideas.py` overwrite cascade (DELETE trade_alert + DELETE trade_journal_notes + UPDATE trade_idea + INSERT alerts + INSERT screenshots + create_note_for_entity + attach_tag_to_entity + _save_ai_conversation_to_idea). Three helpers (`create_note_for_entity`, `attach_tag_to_entity`, `_save_ai_conversation_to_idea`) opened their own `PooledDB` connections, autocommitting independently of the wrapping transaction. Wrapping only the cursor-using portion gave a half-fix that still leaked split-state on cascade failure. The simpler `purge_existing_data` and `upsert_trade_journal` cascades within the same cluster (AUD-0162 + AUD-0163) DID land. **Resolved 2026-05-04 (commit `5a19d9e0`):** all three helpers now accept an optional keyword-only `conn=` parameter. When provided, the helper does NOT open or close its own connection — its writes enrol in the caller's transaction. The standalone path (caller passes nothing) is preserved byte-identical for the 4+ existing route-handler call sites (`ideas.py`, `journal.py`, `tags.py`); no caller migration needed. Inside the helpers, work is extracted into `_create_note_for_entity_with_conn` / `_attach_tag_to_entity_with_conn` / `_save_ai_conversation_to_idea_with_conn` private workers so both call paths share one implementation. Under `conn=` mode, exceptions propagate (instead of being converted to HTTPException 500) so the caller's transaction can roll back; per-message try/except continue in `_save_ai_conversation_to_idea` is also dropped in conn= mode (a swallowed exception inside a PostgreSQL transaction would leave the cursor in an aborted state). The batch_ideas overwrite cascade now calls all three helpers INSIDE the existing manual transaction with `conn=conn`, so any helper failure rolls the entire overwrite back together. Per-helper try/except continue in the cascade is dropped — failures propagate to the cascade-level except which calls rollback. **Intentional asymmetry**: the BATCH-CREATE path keeps the post-commit log-and-continue helper pattern (a failed tag attach should NOT invalidate a new idea — operator can re-attach via the normal UI). The audit was specifically about the OVERWRITE path. Load-bearing comment in batch_ideas.py marks the asymmetry so a future "tidy" doesn't homogenise it. Regression tests: tests/integration/test_aud0118_helper_conn_plumbing.py (10 — 6 source-level signature/structure guards + 4 DB round-trip tests proving caller-conn enrolment for each helper + exception propagation under conn= mode). Full BE suite: 3090 passed (3076 → 3090 = +14, of which 10 are these tests + 4 from the prior AUD-0140 follow-up commit), 4 skipped, no regressions. |

| AUD-0121 | 4 | Major | Bug | Resolved | lib/tradelens/api/trades.py | SL placement inside entry loop | If entry `place_order` raised, SL was never placed and the position stayed open on Bybit without stop. **Resolved 2026-04-26 (commit `f4e571ce`):** SL placement now has a two-call shape — (1) inline call inside the entry-iteration preserves SL-before-TPs ordering for the happy path, satisfying Bybit's per-symbol 10-conditional-order quota safety; (2) post-loop fallback runs as a dedicated step before the response returns when `stop_loss_placed == False` AND any entry/seed/dca leg actually filled — this is the path that closes AUD-0121's bug (e.g., a seeded trade where seed fills but the entry-limit raises so the inline path was skipped). Both call sites use the same `_place_stop_loss_for_intent(...)` helper; the gating ensures SL is placed at most once per trade. New `_rollback_placed_entries(...)` cancels successfully-placed entry legs when a subsequent leg's `place_order` raises (uses `bybit.cancel_order(exchange_order_id)` as primary; falls back to `bybit.cancel_by_order_link_id(order_link_id)` from the AUD-0039 adapter helpers when only the orderLinkId is known — POST-timeout case). Cancel-itself-failures are loud-logged and the original entry error re-raised with context — no live unprotected position is left behind. positionIdx propagates through SL for hedge-mode (long-hedge=1, short-hedge=2). **Note on "lock"**: the audit row's "inside lock" wording was an analogy — there is no Python `threading.Lock` around the entry loop. The atomic boundary is the synchronous request handler itself (return-before-lock-released semantics). A regression test (`test_post_loop_sl_runs_before_response`) pins the SL-fallback-fires-before-response invariant. Public response shape unchanged. AUD-0039's `cancel_by_order_link_id` is exercised by `test_falls_back_to_order_link_id_when_no_exchange_id` — confirms the Tier-3-prerequisite policy works in practice. | AUD-0125 | 4 | Major | Performance | Resolved | lib/tradelens/api/journal.py | `market_summary` | Option (a) landed: `get_market_summary` now resolves current price + four change-windows (15m/1h/4h/1d) for every symbol — including the linear→spot fallback — in a single LATERAL-JOIN round-trip. `unnest(%s::text[])` expands the symbol list, a `VALUES`-table carries the 5 windows (price + 4 historicals), and a `LEFT JOIN LATERAL (… ORDER BY (market_type='linear') DESC, open_time DESC LIMIT 1)` picks the most-recent qualifying candle per (symbol, window) row. Pre-fix the function fired 8-10 distinct `cursor.execute` calls per request (1 price-linear + 1 price-spot fallback + 4 windows × {linear, spot}); now exactly 1. Behaviour preserved: same response shape (`MarketSymbolSummary{price, change_15m, change_1h, change_4h, change_1d}`), same 5-minute tight-window for historical lookups (avoids scanning the 10M-row 1m history), same linear-preferred-then-spot fallback ordering, no staleness (still reads `market_candle` directly, no materialized view). | — | — | Fixed 2026-04-26 (commit 41255fe3 — note: that commit's message references AUD-0283 due to a parallel-session staging-area race; the file content in journal.py + the new test_journal_aud0125_market_summary_single_query.py is the AUD-0125 fix). | AUD-0140 | 4 | Minor | Suspicious | Resolved | lib/tradelens/api/journal.py | 4 state-transition endpoints | **Verification 2026-04-28 (Day 3):** `activate` — 1 mutation (single UPDATE trade_journal) — SAFE. `cancel-seed` — 9 mutations across 8 tables (level_guard, order_leg_live, vwap_linked_order, trade_journal, trade_intent, pending_position_context, vwap_config, trade_journal_notes) — **risky, same class as AUD-0118**. `cancel-pending` — 9 mutations same 8 tables — **risky**. `force-open` — 7 mutations across 4-5 tables — **risky**. The atomic-wrap implementation is non-trivial: each function interleaves Bybit API calls with DB writes; a transaction held across exchange calls = lock contention + long-running tx. Must split into "pre-API DB ops → API call → post-API DB ops" each in its own atomic block. Audit elevated from "Needs verification" to "Confirmed" with concrete scope. | Partial multi-table failure leaves orphaned rows across 4-8 tables; same blast radius as AUD-0118. | Reuse `_atomic_block` from open_orders.py (AUD-0083 helper, ideally lifted to `core/db_helpers.py`). For each endpoint: identify the API-call boundary, split DB writes around it, wrap each side in `_atomic_block`. Targeted integration test per endpoint. | **Resolved 2026-04-29 in two commits.** (1) `_atomic_block` helper LIFTED from `lib/tradelens/api/open_orders.py` to `lib/tradelens/core/db_helpers.py` as `atomic_block`; `open_orders.py` re-exports the old `_atomic_block` name as an alias so every existing call site (lines 1973, 4929) keeps working without churn. (2) **First ship (commit `c5edee16`)** — `cancel_seeded_trade` refactored into Phase A (pre-API atomic_block — read order_leg_live + UPDATE level_guard / DELETE order_leg_live / DELETE vwap_linked_order for guarded LG- orders commit together) → Phase B (Bybit cancels + close_position with autocommit restored, per-order errors captured) → Phase C (post-API atomic_block — UPDATE trade_journal + trade_intent + pending_position_context, DELETE vwap_config + vwap_linked_order, INSERT trade_journal_notes commit together). Test: `tests/integration/test_aud0140_cancel_seed_atomic.py` (6 cases). (3) **Second ship (this commit)** — `cancel_pending_trade` refactored into the same Phase A/B/C shape (no `close_position` branch since pending_entry trades have no fill yet); test: `tests/integration/test_aud0140_cancel_pending_atomic.py` (5 cases). `force_open_trade` got a partial atomic-wrap covering: **Phase 2b** (guarded entry-cancel: 3 DB DELETEs commit together — closes a torn-state window where level_guard/order_leg_live/vwap_linked_order used to autocommit independently), **Phase 2c-fail** (market order rejected: trade_journal status='force_open_failed' UPDATE + INSERT trade_journal_notes commit together so the failure status can't land without its explanatory note), **Phase 2d-fail** (no position-change after market: same status+note atomic), **Phase 5+6** (success path: trade_journal status='open' + trade_intent status='force_opened' + journal note INSERT + auto_tag attach commit together — auto_tag opens its own cursors against `conn` so its writes ride the same transaction). **Phase 3 per-TP loop intentionally PARKED** with documented inline comment + AUD-0218 precedent citation: per-TP Bybit place_order (irreversible, money-moving) interleaves with per-TP DB writes (UPDATE order_leg_live SET lineage_id, create_order_leg INSERT, DELETE vwap_linked_order); a clean transactional wrap would either lose DB tracking on Bybit-success-but-DB-rollback OR convert per-TP partial failures into total force-open rejections. **PERMANENTLY DESCOPED 2026-05-04** (after AUD-0218 Phase 2 shipped): the AUD-0218-style frozen-plan + retry pattern does NOT translate to force_open. Reason — force_open is one-shot (status moves to `'open'` on success; not retryable). A "Retry Force-Open" button would either re-run phases 1+2 (no-ops since the trade is already open with a position) or only re-do phase 3 (placing TPs), which IS literally the normal trade-management "add TP" flow. Building dedicated retry machinery (intermediate state, deterministic per-TP olids, FE Retry button) would duplicate functionality the operator already has. Current shape is correct: TPs that fail to place leave the trade in `'success_degraded'` outcome; operator places replacements via the normal trade-management UI. Future audits encountering this PARK should NOT re-propose option 3 — go straight to "won't fix, see tracker". The smaller adjacent win — wrap the per-TP cancel-loop guarded DELETEs at journal.py:4384-4396 in atomic_block — was shipped in commit `82bb03b1` on 2026-05-04 (closes the 3-DELETE torn-state window for per-TP guarded cancels, mirroring the Phase 2b entry-cancel wrap that already shipped). Test: `tests/integration/test_aud0140_force_open_atomic.py` (6 cases — 4 atomic_block count guard, PARK comment guard, Phase 3 not-wrapped guard, terminal-failure paths inside atomic_block, success path inside atomic_block, behavioural test driving Phase 2c-fail through to a single commit + correct flip sequence). `activate` remains SAFE per original verification — single UPDATE needs no atomic_block. Full suite at close: 2379 passed. **Helper extraction deferred** — cancel-seed and cancel-pending now share ~80% of their Phase A logic; a `_split_and_delete_guarded_orders` helper would clean up duplication but force-open's Phase 2b is slightly different shape (entry-only, level_guard DELETE-by-exchange_order_id rather than UPDATE). 3-call-site helper is the right shape but only after this ship lands. Tracked as follow-up cleanup. |

| AUD-0150 | 5 | Critical | Reliability | Confirmed | bin/pipeline/*.py | no transactions anywhere | `conn.commit` / `conn.rollback` / BEGIN / COMMIT / ROLLBACK → 0 hits across 8,349 LOC. | `upsert_trade_journal` cascades into pending_context, alerts, idea-copy, vwap-linked updates — mid-stream failure leaves inconsistent state. | Per-session transaction with savepoint. | all three files. **2026-04-25 (cluster sweep): partial-stop**. The cluster's "pipeline-archive" sub-path is `archive_disappeared_order` in `bin/pipeline/refresh_order_leg_live.py:1434-1622`. Wrapping it end-to-end is unsafe: the function interleaves DB writes with **Bybit HTTP calls** — `bybit.get_order_history()` at line 1482 to fetch the order's terminal state, plus `_check_breakeven_trigger` at line 1614 which can call `bybit.amend_order()` to move SL to break-even. Holding a DB transaction open across HTTP calls is a known anti-pattern (locks held while we wait on a network round-trip; if the Bybit call hangs the txn slot stays occupied). The function's existing structure DELIBERATELY makes the archive step (INSERT order_leg_hist) and the delete step (DELETE order_leg_live) **independent** writes precisely so a transient Bybit failure doesn't poison the DB. A safe wrap point would be a tighter scope (just the `upsert_hist_legs_to_db([leg], …)` call inside `_archive_from_live_snapshot`) but that is a single-statement INSERT, not a multi-statement cascade — so wrapping it in a transaction is a no-op vs. the existing autocommit. AUD-0150 stays Confirmed pending an architectural rework that splits the Bybit-fetch and DB-write phases (e.g. fetch-all-stale-orders-into-memory first, then a separate DB-only loop with explicit txn). The two refresh_trade_journal pipeline writes from the same cluster (AUD-0162 + AUD-0163) DID land; AUD-0150's broader scope (all three pipeline scripts) is best handled per-function once the shared base in AUD-0168 lands. |

Resolved 2026-04-24: deleted whole module (134 LOC). Re-verified zero callers in lib/, bin/, tests/ before delete. Pytest remains green. |

| AUD-0156 | 5 | Major | Suspicious | Resolved | bin/pipeline/refresh_order_leg_live.py | `ThreadPoolExecutor` sharing `self.bybit` and writing to `self.positions_map` | Concurrent Bybit fetches write back to classifier state. | Thread safety relies on `httpx.Client` thread-safety + main-thread accumulation pattern. | Document invariants; add assertions. | refresh_order_leg_live.py:352, 398, 450. Verified 2026-04-25: closed as WAI. The audit description is wrong about the write pattern — `self.positions_map` is only written in `fetch_context()` (single site at L131) which runs on the main thread BEFORE any ThreadPoolExecutor is constructed. All 3 thread pools (linear/inverse/spot at L372/425/481) only READ `positions_map`. `httpx.Client` is documented thread-safe in httpx 0.28.1 (per-request state is built as locals in `_request()`). `BybitClient` instance attrs are read-only after construction. Pattern is correct. |

| AUD-0163 | 5 | Major | Reliability | Resolved | bin/pipeline/refresh_trade_journal.py | `upsert_trade_journal` cascades | INSERT + 4-5 follow-ups (pending context, alerts, idea-copy, vwap-linked) without transaction or idempotency guard. | Re-running pipeline may duplicate idea-copy items. | Transaction + upsert idempotency. | refresh_trade_journal.py:1648-2255. Resolved 2026-04-25: wrapped `upsert_trade_journal` (530-line body, two return paths) in `_wrap_upsert_in_transaction` decorator so the INSERT/UPDATE plus its cascades (idea-item copy, pending_position_context update, vwap_linked_order update, trade_alert expire, attach_*_tag_if_needed) commit atomically. Decorator pattern chosen over inline try/except because the latter would have required re-indenting the whole body and breaking AUD-0148 / AUD-0152 / AUD-0153 source-scanning regression tests. Decorator is autocommit-aware: when called with a connection that already has autocommit=False (e.g. the rollback-based `test_db_conn` fixture) it passes through without touching the txn boundary. Idempotency on re-runs: existing call-site guards (intent_update only fires when trade_intent_id was previously NULL; INSERT-path idea-copy only fires on first creation; copy_idea_items_to_trade has its own per-item dedup) are sufficient — no new guards needed beyond the txn wrap. | AUD-0186 | 6 | Critical | Bug | Resolved | bin/levelguard_cli.py | broken path resolution at its bin/ location | **Correction:** `bin/levelguard_cli.py` was a symlink to `tools/levelguard_cli.py` (confirmed at the pre-deletion commit: `git show HEAD~1:tradelens/bin/levelguard_cli.py` prints the target path, not file content). | AUD-0217 | 7 | Critical | Reliability | Resolved | lib/tradelens/api/batch_ideas.py | `batch_create_ideas` overwrite has no transaction | DELETE trade_alert + DELETE trade_journal_notes + UPDATE trade_idea + 5 side-effects ran on autocommit. **Resolved 2026-04-26 (cluster commit `306af910`):** the local-cursor portion of the overwrite block (DELETE trade_alert + DELETE trade_journal_notes + UPDATE trade_idea + `_insert_entry_alerts` + `_save_images_as_screenshots`) now runs inside a single `autocommit=False` transaction. Mid-cascade failure rolls back atomically and re-raises. Three side-effect helpers (`create_note_for_entity`, `attach_tag_to_entity`, `_save_ai_conversation_to_idea`) open their own pooled connections via `PooledDB(...)` so they can't join the handler's transaction without refactoring multiple caller surfaces — they keep the prior log-and-continue contract (documented inline as a scope-expansion park). Pre-existing `try/except continue` swallows for `_insert_entry_alerts` / `_save_images_as_screenshots` were removed because in `autocommit=False` mode psycopg2 leaves the cursor ABORTED on swallowed errors — the next statement would fail anyway, and the brief's "atomic rollback" semantics explicitly want failure to propagate. | AUD-0218 | 7 | Critical | Reliability | Resolved | lib/tradelens/api/suspend.py | suspend/resume/close intra-lock autocommit | AppLock held but per-step DB writes were autocommit; hence SUSPEND PARTIAL FAILURE was a documented mode. **Phase 1 (suspend/close) Resolved 2026-04-26 (commit `306af910`):** `suspend_trade` and `close_trade` per-handler write cascades now run inside `autocommit=False` transactions strictly within the existing AppLock's scope. The SUSPEND-PARTIAL-FAILURE intra-request torn-state mode is closed by atomic rollback. Behaviour change (intentional): pre-fix the trade was left in `'suspending'` on partial failure; post-fix rollback un-claims the CAS row and the trade returns to `'open'`, retry-safe. **Phase 2 (resume) Resolved 2026-05-04** (5 commits: b9ef9967 schema + design doc → f93eb44d helpers → e2de130b handler refactor → 4faef01e duplicate-olid recovery → final FE + status-canonical). Design doc `docs/30-fixes-and-audits/audits/audit-autofix/2026-05-04-aud-0218-resume-design.md` — 7 locked decisions: pause-on-error with manual retry; freeze surviving_orders on first attempt + reload on retry; query order_leg_live by (trade_id, lineage_id) to skip already-placed legs; treat duplicate-orderLinkId Bybit response as success and recover orderId via get_open_orders + olid filter; keep entry market order on partial failure; manual-only (no auto-revert from 'resuming'); same Resume button (label flips to "Retry Resume"); AUD-0229 dual-write extended to terminal 'resuming'. (3) `resume_trade` refactored: status gate widened to ('suspended','resuming'); plan-resolution wrapped in `atomic_block` + delegated to load_or_freeze; per-leg loop prepended with `if is_retry and leg_already_placed(...)` skip; per-leg place call wrapped in `try/except ExchangeError` with duplicate-olid recovery branch (new statuses 'RecoveredFromOrphan' + 'OrphanedOnExchange'); partial-failure path writes `status='resuming'` with AUD-0229 dual-write to status_enum AND persists resume_failed_idx + resume_last_error inside a single atomic_block; full-success path clears retry state + frozen plan inside a single atomic_block. | AUD-0243 | 8 | Critical | Performance | Resolved | lib/tradelens/api/discord_ingest.py | synchronous image downloads in request path | Serial `urlopen(..., timeout=15)` per attachment per message in the handler. **Resolved 2026-04-26 (option b — thread-pool parallelism, after option-a investigation showed BG tasks would race with synchronous downstream consumers):** the pre-AUD-0254 inline serial loop (and post-AUD-0254 single download site at `_run_message_pipeline:402-410`) was replaced with a new module-level helper `_download_image_attachments_parallel` that submits all per-message HTTP image attachments to a `concurrent.futures.ThreadPoolExecutor` (max_workers = `min(10, len(image_atts))`, capped by module constant `_IMAGE_DOWNLOAD_MAX_WORKERS = 10` matching Discord's per-message attachment limit). The pool is awaited synchronously BEFORE `handler.handle()` runs for that message, so the synchronous contract that downstream consumers depend on is preserved: (a) `discord/parser.py:148-160` flips between text-only and gpt-4o vision based on `image_path` resolving to an existing local file; (b) `discord/idea_creator.py:661-670:attach_image` reads the local file path before writing the `trade_journal_notes` snapshot row; (c) `discord/state_machine_handler.py` checks `Path(url).exists()` on the leg. A first sub-agent investigated option (a) FastAPI BackgroundTasks and correctly aborted because BG tasks would race with all three of those consumers; option (b) — same call graph, parallel I/O — collapses 10 × 15s serial → ~15s wall while keeping the consumers' inputs intact. Failures (exception, `None` return) leave `att["url"]` unchanged at the original HTTP URL, matching the prior serial loop's best-effort behaviour; the worker also catches stray exceptions internally so a single failing attachment can't crash the per-message loop. The `is_image` predicate (`content_type.startswith("image/") OR url ends in known raster ext`) was lifted into a small named helper `_is_image_attachment` to keep the parallel filter bytes-identical to the prior inline check. Reuses the existing `_download_discord_image` worker unchanged. Response shape unchanged. Regression test: `tests/integration/test_aud0243_thread_pool_image_downloads.py` (7 tests covering parallel dispatch + multi-thread, mutation contract success/failure, handler-runs-after-downloads ordering, no-op short-circuit for empty / non-image / non-HTTP, and per-future failure containment when one worker raises). | Blocks API worker threads; at concurrency > pool size the API stalls. | BackgroundTasks or thread-pool parallelism. | discord_ingest.py:325-333, 434-441. |
| AUD-0244 | 8 | Critical | Reliability | Resolved | lib/tradelens/discord/idea_creator.py | create_idea cascade no transaction | Idea + note + tags + images + URL-screenshots all autocommitted; each step had its own try/except continue-on-failure → partial idea with no note/tags was possible. **Resolved 2026-04-26 (commit `797b5060`):** `create_idea` is now split into pre-write validation (no DB writes; legacy `return None` contract preserved for bad direction / bad symbol / dedup hit / dry-run) and a transactional write cascade. The cascade (idea INSERT → attach_note → attach_tags → attach_image × N → attach_url_screenshot × N) runs inside a single `autocommit=False` transaction per message. Success → `conn.commit()`. Any exception → `conn.rollback()` + log with channel/msg-id/symbol context + re-raise. `finally` restores `conn.autocommit` to its pre-call value (mirrors AUD-0211 / AUD-0184 / AUD-0163). If the connection is already `autocommit=False` (caller-managed, e.g. test rollback fixture), the function passes through without touching the boundary. Inbox-log moved OUTSIDE the transaction so a swallowed inbox failure can't poison the transaction state and silently roll back a successful idea. **Per-message scope** — verified by the multi-message-loop test: 3 messages, message 2 fails mid-cascade → messages 1 and 3 fully persist, message 2 has zero rows. The outer `discord_ingest.py:502-510` per-message try/except already catches and continues, matching the contract. Caller files (`handler.py`, `state_machine_handler.py`, `discord_ingest.py`) untouched. Mirrors AUD-0211 / AUD-0184 transaction-shape pattern. Reinforces AUD-0118 deduplication semantics. Regression tests: tests/integration/test_aud0244_idea_create_transaction.py (8 — happy path persists full cascade; autocommit restoration; per-step failure rollback at idea / note / tag / image / url-screenshot; no-orphan-rows on idea-INSERT failure; multi-message loop per-message scope). Sweep `pytest -k "aud0244 or idea_creator or discord_ingest"`: 29 passed. | Partial idea with no note/tags is possible. Reinforces AUD-0118. | Single transaction over cascade. | idea_creator.py:899-1100. |

| AUD-0271 | 9 | Critical | Performance | Resolved | lib/tradelens/candle_pg/store_pg.py | `upsert_candles` per-row UPDATE/INSERT | Comment claims batch existence check; writes were per-row. **Resolved 2026-04-26 (commit `220e645d`):** rewrote `upsert_candles` from a per-candle UPDATE/INSERT loop to a single `INSERT … ON CONFLICT (symbol, market_type, timeframe, open_time) DO UPDATE SET …` using `psycopg2.extras.execute_values` (page_size=1000). N round-trips per batch collapse to 1. Three-branch semantics from the original loop preserved in one SQL statement: existing-closed rows are skipped via `WHERE market_candle.is_closed = FALSE`, existing-open + new-closed get a full overwrite, and existing-open + new-open preserves `c_open` via `CASE WHEN EXCLUDED.is_closed THEN EXCLUDED.c_open ELSE market_candle.c_open END`. `created_at` deliberately omitted from SET so it is preserved on update. (inserted, updated) counters reproduced via `RETURNING (xmax = 0)` — skipped immutable rows don't appear in RETURNING so semantics match the per-row implementation byte-for-byte. Function signature, return type, exception behaviour, and connection-acquisition pattern all unchanged (per-thread connections is AUD-0272 step A territory, deliberately out of scope). Misleading "batch existence check" comment removed. The on-disk `etc/schema.md` is stale (still references Sybase-era `market_candle_DISABLED`); the authoritative shape is `migrations/078_market_candle_pg_schema.sql` which sets the PRIMARY KEY used by ON CONFLICT. Regression tests: tests/integration/test_aud0271_candle_upsert_batched.py (5 — fresh-insert 100 candles, update-on-key-collision, mixed insert+update merge, empty-batch no-op, single-round-trip lock-in via cursor.execute spy). Sweep `pytest -k "candle or store_pg or aud0271"`: 44 passed; mdsync/runner unit regression: 25 passed; AUD-0270 regression: 6 passed. | N round-trips per batch; dominates mdsync live loop. | `INSERT ... ON CONFLICT DO UPDATE` with `execute_values`. | store_pg.py:104-220. |
| AUD-0272 | 9 | Critical | Performance | Resolved (partial) | lib/tradelens/mdsync/runner.py | parallel fetch + serial upsert on single PG conn | 10-worker fetch thread pool but one PG connection for upserts. | Upsert phase doesn't scale; hardcoded `MAIN_LOOP_WORKERS=10`, `LIVE_LOOP_INTERVAL_SECONDS=10`. | Batch upsert (C5 fix) or per-thread connections. | Resolved (partial) 2026-04-26: focused half of the audit row's two-part recommendation landed. The hardcoded polling cadence (`MAIN_LOOP_WORKERS`, `LIVE_LOOP_INTERVAL_SECONDS`) is now config-driven via `etc/config.yml` → `market_data.tuning` (defaults 10/10 match pre-fix literals; behaviour byte-identical when config is unset). The `_load_runner_tuning` loader gained AUD-0272 validation: any non-positive-int override (zero, negative, non-int, bool) is logged as a warning and replaced with the default so an operator typo can't wedge the daemon (interval=0 would busy-spin; workers=0 would crash ThreadPoolExecutor). Module-level `MAIN_LOOP_WORKERS` and `LIVE_LOOP_INTERVAL_SECONDS` bindings preserved for backward-compat. **Update 2026-04-26 (step E follow-up — commit `f4c40aeb`):** opt-in profile instrumentation added so an operator can validate the upsert-dominates premise before step A (per-thread connections + pool bump) ships. New flag `market_data.tuning.profile_aud0272` (bool, default false). When true, `_update_live_candles` wraps fetch + upsert loops with `time.perf_counter()` and emits per-cycle structured INFO logs prefixed `AUD-0272-PROFILE cycle=N symbols=… fetch_total=…s upsert_total=…s ratio=… candles=…` for clean grep'ability. When false, instrumentation short-circuits at one bool check (no perf_counter calls, no log volume). Bool-only validation in `_load_runner_tuning` (non-bool falls back to false with warning). Tests: `tests/unit/test_aud0272_profile_instrumentation.py` (14 — short-circuit zero-overhead path; emits the AUD-0272-PROFILE summary; required keys; ratio math; ZeroDivisionError handling for zero-symbol cycles; bool-only config validation). Two AUD-0283 fixture-dict assertions updated additively to include the new key. Step A (per-thread connections + pool_max bump) is conditional on this profiling validating the premise during a soak window.

**Out of scope for this commit** (deliberately not addressed): the audit's broader recommendation — "batch upsert OR per-thread connections" — is a separate architectural concern about scaling the upsert path on a single PG connection, and remains a candidate for a future T3-sized refactor. The infrastructure to retune workers from config (without the underlying connection-model change) is what shipped here. Note: the literal→config move for these two specific keys was originally landed by AUD-0283 (commit `8f7abdfa`); this commit adds the AUD-0272 validation layer + an AUD-0272-named regression net that pins both the cadence defaults and the new validation contract. | AUD-0280 | 9 | Major | Cleanup | Resolved | lib/tradelens/api/vwap.py | vwap_config.slots_json opaque JSON blob | 3-slot config stored as opaque TEXT JSON; no structured query. **Resolved 2026-04-26 (commit `966e75df`):** migration `082_vwap_config_slots_jsonb.sql` shipped option A — `slots_json` column converted from TEXT/JSON to JSONB; `CREATE INDEX IF NOT EXISTS idx_vwap_config_slots_gin USING GIN (slots_json jsonb_path_ops)` enables structured `@>` containment queries. Forward-only idempotent. Data-shape rationale: all 177 production rows share the same nested 3-slot shape, but the `VwapSlotConfig` Pydantic model has gained fields incrementally — typed-column flattening would lock the schema and require a fresh migration per Pydantic addition; JSONB preserves the dict shape with structured-query support. Pre-flight cast probe (`r.slots_json::jsonb`) confirmed all 177 prod rows cast cleanly with zero failures (production untouched in this ship; only `tradelens_test` had the migration applied per the standing decision). **Hidden silent-regression mitigated**: psycopg2 returns JSONB as `dict`, not `str`. Every existing read site called `json.loads(row[0])` which would have raised TypeError → caught by exception handler returning DEFAULT config → silent loss of every user's VWAP slot configuration. Plus three read-then-write sites (`update_cached_timeframe`, `idea_item_copier.copy_vwap_config`, `ideas.py` copy-from-trade) would have raised `psycopg2.ProgrammingError: can't adapt type 'dict'` on writeback. Fix: `parse_slots_value(None|str|dict) -> dict|None` helper in `lib/tradelens/utils/vwap_calculator.py`; all readers call it; writers re-serialise dict → JSON string before INSERT/UPDATE. **Side-fix (in scope, security)**: `update_cached_timeframe` had pre-existing f-string SQL injection (`SET slots_json = '{new_json}', updated_at = ... WHERE trade_id = {trade_id}`); switching to parameterised form was unavoidable when changing the JSON serialisation, so it ships with the JSONB migration. Schema reflected in `bin/setup/setup_database_pg.py` and `etc/schema.md`. Files touched: 9 (migration + test + 7 read/write sites). Regression tests: tests/integration/test_aud0280_vwap_config_jsonb.py (5 — slots_json is JSONB, GIN index with jsonb_path_ops exists, round-trip preserves data, idempotency, JSONB `@>` containment query works). | AUD-0281 | 9 | Major | Reliability | Resolved | bin/server/level_mind_worker.py | background lease-refresh task for long-running worker jobs (option a) | **2026-04-26 reconciliation note: ID re-purposed.** The original AUD-0281 row (per audit chunks 9-14) was a *positive* Confirmed observation — `bin/engine/vwap_order_engine.py + vwap_series_worker.py` correctly use `singleton_lock` and were flagged as the good-pattern source for AUD-0182 to propagate. AUD-0182 shipped 2026-04-23 (commit `6f81695b`) propagating flock to LevelGuard / level_mind / pipeline daemons, which closed the original concern as WAI. The XL-batch sub-agent then re-purposed AUD-0281 to track a separate concern (lease-refresh watchdog for level_mind_worker) and shipped that fix; both the original WAI-confirmation and the new lease-watchdog work are captured here. — Resolved 2026-04-26. Pre-fix the lease was renewed inline at the top of each monitor's work loop (`level_mind_worker.py:756-775`); a single iteration longer than `LEASE_WINDOW_SECONDS` (e.g., a slow `core.evaluate()`, a stalled HTTP fetch, or a long internal sleep) would silently let the lease expire and another worker could claim ownership while this monitor kept writing under a stolen lease. Fix: added `_start_lease_watchdog()` (level_mind_worker.py:535-616) — a daemon thread that calls `_refresh_lease()` every `LEASE_REFRESH_SECONDS` regardless of where the work loop is. The watchdog signals ownership loss to the monitor via a `lease_lost_event`; the monitor checks the event at the top of each loop iteration and breaks out (level_mind_worker.py:863-874). Cleanup in the `finally` block joins the watchdog before returning the connection to the pool so a final tick can't fire UPDATE on a connection now owned by another thread (level_mind_worker.py:1054-1072). Regression test: tests/unit/test_aud0281_lease_watchdog.py (4 cases: timer fires on interval, stops cleanly on stop_event, signals ownership loss, refreshes during a blocked job — the central regression). | AUD-0292 | 10 | Critical | Reliability | Resolved | bin/server/start_api.sh + daemon wrappers | unbounded force-kill loops | `while pgrep; pkill -9; sleep` has no max iterations or timeout. | Kernel-uninterruptible D-state process can hang `start` scripts forever. | Bounded retry count with alert on failure. | Resolved 2026-04-26 (option a). The three launchers carrying the unbounded `while pgrep ... pkill -9 ... sleep ... done` loop (`bin/server/start_api.sh`, `bin/server/stop_api.sh`, `bin/server/start_trade_dashboard.sh` — last one had two copies for uvicorn + vite) now route through a single shared helper at `bin/lib/kill_helpers.sh` (`bounded_pkill_pattern <pattern> <label>`). The helper sends SIGTERM, polls for up to `TL_FORCE_KILL_TIMEOUT` seconds (same env var as AUD-0305, default 5), then SIGKILLs anything that survived, and finally re-checks; if a process STILL refuses to die, the helper logs a WARNING to stderr and returns non-zero so the launcher exits with a clear error rather than silently spinning forever. The audit row's `alert-engine:92-95; level-guard:90-95` references are out of scope for this option-a fix — those wrappers already use a `kill ... sleep 5 ... kill -9` graceful-then-force pattern (just without configurable timeout). The remaining `pkill -f` substring weakness called out by the audit row is AUD-0293's territory (PID-file first; pgrep fallback) and is intentionally left to that batch. Regression test: tests/unit/test_aud0292_bounded_kill.py (18 cases — source-text guards on all three launchers, helper contract pins for SIGTERM-then-SIGKILL ordering and TL_FORCE_KILL_TIMEOUT plumbing, fast-path/no-match short-circuit, friendly-child SIGTERM happy path, SIGTERM-deaf-child SIGKILL escalation, env-var timing diff, empty-pattern guard). Full suite: 1205 passed, 4 skipped. |
| AUD-0293 | 10 | Critical | Security | Resolved | bin/*/shell wrappers | unqualified `pkill -f` command-line matching | All `pgrep -f` / `pkill -f` patterns across the bin/ shell wrappers are now path-qualified so two installs on the same host cannot cross-match. **`bin/lib/service_wrapper.sh`**: introduced `_AUTORESTART_PATTERN` (`${TLHOME}/bin/lib/autorestart\.sh.*--name ${SERVICE_NAME}( \|$)`) and `_QUALIFIED_PROC_PATTERN` (`${TLHOME}/.*${SERVICE_PROC_PATTERN}`) module-level vars; every `pgrep -f` site (start defensive check, stop fallback, stop child reap, status fallback) now uses one of these. The `( \|$)` end-anchor on the autorestart pattern prevents substring collisions like `--name level-guard` matching `--name level-mind`. **`bin/server/start_api.sh` + `stop_api.sh`**: `bounded_pkill_pattern "${TSHOME}/venv/bin/uvicorn tradelens.main:app"` instead of bare `"uvicorn tradelens.main:app"` substring. **`bin/server/start_trade_dashboard.sh`**: same uvicorn fix + `bounded_pkill_pattern "${TLHOME}/frontend/web/node_modules/.bin/vite.*--port"` for vite. **`bin/server/stop_trade_dashboard.sh`**: derives TSHOME from TLHOME at top, then anchors orphan `pgrep` for uvicorn on `${TSHOME}/venv/bin/uvicorn` and vite on `${TLHOME}/frontend/web/node_modules/.bin/vite`. PID-file remains the primary path; pgrep is the documented fallback for orphan / no-PID-file states. Verified end-to-end against live processes on rocky-8gb (alert-engine, telegram-signals, uvicorn, vite all match new patterns; cross-install false-positives no longer match). | Two tradelens installs on same host (staging + prod) → `stop` kills both. | PID-file first; pgrep fallback with path qualification. | start_api.sh:103; all wrappers. | AUD-0341 | 13 | Critical | Performance | Resolved | lib/tradelens/api/system_monitor.py | 30+ subprocess spawns per request, no caching | Each `/system-monitor` hit runs `free -m` ×2, `df`, `ps`/`pgrep` per service × ~13, `os.listdir /proc/<pid>/fd` per service. Frontend polls it. | ~180 subprocess execs/sec/worker under polling; fork overhead dominates. | Cache 2-3s. | system_monitor.py:95-345. **Reclassified 2026-04-26 → bucket C (money-adjacent, schema change required when bundled with AUD-0343)**. **Resolved 2026-05-04 (cache half only, decoupled from AUD-0343 bundle):** the AUD-0341 portion is the per-request fork cost, which a TTL cache solves without any schema work. The AUD-0343 bundle (scorecard `source_channel_key` migration + parser updates) remains a separate effort. Implementation: `_collect_system_monitor_response()` extracted from the route handler; the `/system-monitor` route is now a thin TTL-cache wrapper with `_CACHE_TTL_SECONDS = 2.5` and a `threading.Lock` for single-flight semantics. Concurrent misses funnel into one collection; followers return the cached response. `/system-monitor/history/{service_name}` is intentionally NOT cached. No new dependencies (the recommendation's `psutil` half was dropped as unnecessary — the helpers are already mostly /proc-based after AUD-0350). Cap on per-second cost is now O(1 collection / 2.5 s) regardless of poll rate; with the frontend polling at 10 s, every visible refresh still sees a fresh collection. Tests: 4 unit tests in `tests/unit/test_aud0341_system_monitor_cache.py` covering cache hit, cache expiry, concurrent single-flight, and history-endpoint regression. AUD-0350 regression test (`test_aud0350_system_monitor_proc_atomic.py`) re-run and still green. Full BE gate: 3074 passed, 4 skipped. |

| AUD-0350 | 13 | Major | Reliability | Resolved | lib/tradelens/api/system_monitor.py | TOCTOU between PID read and metrics collection | **Resolved 2026-04-29 (Wave 3B commit `bb087cff`):** `get_process_metrics` now reads `/proc/<pid>/status` atomically for RSS + threads. The pre-fix `ps -o rss=,%cpu=,nlwp= -p <pid>` subprocess (one of the audit's "3 subprocess round-trips") is gone. FileNotFoundError / ProcessLookupError / PermissionError / OSError on the /proc open() returns all-None metrics — graceful stale-PID handling, no risk of attaching to a possibly-reused PID. The /proc/<pid>/fd directory listing (FD count) keeps its independent try/except so a between-reads death gives partial-result rather than zero-result. CPU% intentionally remains on `ps -o %cpu= -p <pid>` because /proc/stat-based delta requires sampling twice over an interval (different semantics); CPU% ps call is now isolated (own try/except, own subprocess) so its own TOCTOU risk doesn't poison rss/threads/fds. Regression tests: tests/unit/test_aud0350_system_monitor_proc_atomic.py (5 — dead-PID returns all-None, source-shape guard for /proc/<pid>/status read + VmRSS/Threads parsers, source-shape guard against the combined `ps -o rss=,%cpu=,nlwp=` argv, PermissionError on open() returns all-None, end-to-end mock with fake /proc content verifying VmRSS scaling kB→MB and Threads parsing). Engine daemons (alert_engine, correlation_worker, vwap_series_worker, vwap_order_engine) wired to call the helper after their existing `setup_logging()` call. mdsync_pg + telegram_signals install `RotatingFileHandler` inline because their cold-start `setup_logging` runs before the tradelens lib is on sys.path. Defaults match AUD-0209 (50 MB/file × 10 backups → ~550 MB total per daemon). Audit's "8 daemons" was 6 in practice — `monitor` is bash (no Python logging) and `discord_signals.py` no longer exists (Discord ingest moved to browser extension in April 2026). Deployed to rocky2 via git pull + mdsync_pg restart 2026-04-29 20:32Z. Regression tests: tests/unit/test_aud0371_log_rotation_daemons.py (16 — helper presence + AUD-0209 constants, end-to-end rotation triggered by tiny maxBytes, idempotency, parametrized source-shape per daemon, AST guard against bare FileHandler() in any of the 6). | — | — | Resolved via shared helper + 6-daemon wire. |

| AUD-0373 | 16 | Major | Bug | Resolved (duplicate) | bin/server/level_guard_daemon.py | `_set_guard_failed` broken constructor call | Calls `GuardStateData(state=GuardState.CANCELLED)` without the required `config: GuardConfig` arg → raises TypeError on every invocation. The TypeError is swallowed by the surrounding `try/except` and logged as a warning ("Failed to update guard state for leg N"). Result: the function NEVER updates `guard_state_json` to mark the leg CANCELLED, even though that's its entire purpose. The function does NOT delete the leg, so the broken update is operationally meaningful — daemon expects `guard_state_json.state=CANCELLED` to skip the leg on next cycle. Latent since commit 74412843 (March 2026, auto-suspend feature). | Daemon may re-attempt the failed guard on every cycle instead of skipping it. Silent reliability issue masked by the swallowed TypeError. | Either pass a stub `GuardConfig` to the constructor, OR audit whether the cycle-skip works via some other path (e.g., `guard_state_json.state` already at a terminal value before this function runs). Found by AUD-0211 sub-agent 2026-04-25. | **2026-04-26: Duplicate of AUD-0367, which was already fixed in commit `b50641ed` on 2026-04-25 — opened in 93c65abb tracker batch the same day without realising AUD-0367 had already shipped the fix. No-op resolution.** Same code structure exists in `_cancel_guard_and_leg` and was fixed under AUD-0211 (commit `e50d5894`) by removing the broken call entirely (the row is deleted on the next statement so the update was a no-op anyway). ## Parked items (long-term)

Items here are **deliberately on hold for months or longer**, blocked on
external prerequisites the operator has named. Different from "Confirmed"
(real issue, not yet scheduled) or "Resolved (partial)" (work in progress
with a follow-up commit pending in the near term). When the named blocker
clears, move the item out of this section back into normal flow.

### AUD-0227 Phase 3 + Phase 4 — blocked on sender domain

**Parked:** 2026-04-30
**Blocker:** Operator does not own a sender domain (e.g. `tradelens.io`)
and is not expected to acquire one for several months. Without a domain,
no transactional email can send (verification, password-reset,
confirmation) — Phase 3 and Phase 4 cannot start.

**What's parked:**
- **Phase 3** — self-signup + email verification + password reset.
  Design doc shipped at
  `docs/30-fixes-and-audits/audits/audit-autofix/2026-04-30-aud-0227-phase3-design.md`
  (commit `46eb2979`); 12-question spec; 8-commit implementation plan
  (3.1 schema 093 → 3.2 email infra → 3.3 token+rate-limit → 3.4 verify
  flow → 3.5 password reset → 3.6 invite subsystem → 3.7 FE pages → 3.8
  cutover). Q1 picks Resend as provider; Q2 (sender domain) is the
  blocking question.
- **Phase 4** — per-user IP routing, billing, multi-tenant rate-limit
  isolation, 2FA (TOTP / WebAuthn / passkeys), OAuth / social login.
  No design doc yet; downstream of Phase 3 (no point planning Phase 4
  while signup is unbuilt). Trigger to start: operational scale demands
  per-tenant isolation OR a SaaS-launch decision firms up.

**What still works in the parked state:**
- Phase 1 + Phase 2 are fully shipped and on production. Operator-issued
  user creation via `bin/setup/manage_users.py create / reset-pwd`
  remains the only onboarding path; encrypted Bybit credentials are
  per-user. There is no functional gap for the single-operator
  deployment.
- AUD-0227 row status is "Resolved (partial)" reflecting Phase 1+2
  closure; the row will move to "Resolved" only when Phase 3 ships.

**Revisit when:** operator acquires a sender domain (or chooses an
alternative path like SES + a known mailbox). At that point, lock
Q1–Q12 in the Phase 3 design doc, ship the 8 commits, then evaluate
Phase 4.

**Related rows:** AUD-0312 (Resolved as side-effect of Phase 1),
AUD-0112 (Resolved before Phase 1).

## Follow-up waves — operator action paths (post-2026-04-28 campaign)

Recorded at the close of the 3-day audit-fix campaign (commits `1e99d0f3 …
b7f081a5`, full report at
`docs/30-fixes-and-audits/audits/audit-autofix/2026-04-28-3day-campaign-final.md`).
Each entry below bundles parked items into one operator-actionable wave so a
future session can pick it up without re-discovering the scope.

### Wave A — AppLock + orderLinkId (open_orders.py + bybit_client.py) — CLOSED ✅

**Items:** AUD-0079 ✅, AUD-0081 ✅, AUD-0082 ✅, AUD-0083 LevelGuard CREATE-path remainder ✅.

**Status (Campaign 2 Day 1, post-`ac17e4df`):** Wave A is **fully closed**.
All four audits flipped to Resolved across the campaign's wave. The
wrap-then-`_<endpoint>_locked`-helper pattern is established across all
four mutation endpoints in `open_orders.py` and is the canonical shape
for any future endpoint that needs the same treatment.

**Shipped (in order):**
- **AUD-0079** (`51f02b6e`): `BybitClient.cancel_batch_orders` +
  `bulk_cancel_orders` rewrite with classification (LG-local /
  conditional-TP-per-order / simple-batchable) + single-refresh-at-end.
- **AUD-0083 LevelGuard CREATE remainder** (`51f02b6e`): `_atomic_block`
  applied to the CREATE path; level_guard log-warning swallow removed;
  rollback returns `CreateOrderResponse(success=False, ...)`.
- **AUD-0082** (`b8674f35`): orderLinkId pre-generated via
  `_generate_order_link_id(trade_id, leg_kind)` at all 4 placement
  callsites; passed explicitly; logged for safe-retry recovery;
  persisted into `order_leg_live.order_link_id` at each corresponding
  INSERT/UPDATE. LG CREATE path skipped (LG orders never hit Bybit
  place_order).
- **AUD-0081 (cancel + convert)** (`829f2405`): `cancel_order` and
  `convert_to_limit` wrapped in AppLock with per-leg lock_key, role
  tags 'cancel' / 'convert-to-limit'.
- **AUD-0081 residual (amend + create)** (`ac17e4df`): `amend_order`
  wrapped (per-leg lock_key, role='amend'); the inner AppLock at the
  disable-LG subpath replaced with `contextlib.nullcontext()` to
  preserve the ~600-line indented body. `create_order` wrapped with
  composite lock_key `f'create-trade-{trade_id}-{order_type}-{order_kind}'`
  so same-button double-clicks contend while concurrent multi-leg
  setup (entry + SL + TP) proceeds in parallel; role='create'.

**Pattern (canonical) for future mutation endpoints:**

```python
@router.post("...")
def public_endpoint(request, background_tasks=None, ...):
    """Brief docstring; mention AppLock + lock_key choice."""
    try:
        with AppLock(
            namespace='order-mutation',
            lock_key=f'<your-key>',
            lock_type='exclusive',
            ttl_seconds=30,
            wait_seconds=2,
            role='<role-tag>',
        ):
            return _public_endpoint_locked(request, background_tasks, ...)
    except LockAcquireError:
        raise HTTPException(
            status_code=409,
            detail="Resource is currently being modified — please retry",
        )

def _public_endpoint_locked(request, background_tasks=None, ...):
    """AUD-0081 internal helper: body of public_endpoint, runs under lock."""
    # ...original body unchanged...
```

This pattern keeps the locking concern outside the body, avoids
re-indenting long endpoint implementations, and gives observability
roles for monitoring lock contention by mutation type.

**Wave A residual:** none. Closed cleanly.

### Wave C — Multi-table transaction wrap — CLOSED ✅

All three Wave C items shipped:

- **AUD-0140** (cancel-seed, cancel-pending, force-open in journal.py)
  — shipped 2026-04-29 (commits c5edee16 + force-open partial wrap, see
  AUD-0140 row). Per-TP cancel-loop guarded DELETEs additionally wrapped
  2026-05-04 (commit 82bb03b1). Per-TP PLACE loop permanently descoped
  in same commit (one-shot semantics — see AUD-0140 row).
- **AUD-0218** (resume_trade two-phase) — shipped 2026-05-04 with
  pause-on-error + manual retry (5 commits b9ef9967 → final FE).
  Decision was pause-on-error (not commit-or-compensate); the
  per-leg loop wraps DB inserts in atomic_block but keeps Bybit calls
  outside the transaction, with frozen-plan retries handling the
  cross-attempt idempotency.
- **AUD-0118** (batch_ideas overwrite cascade — helper conn= plumbing)
  — shipped 2026-05-04 (this commit). `create_note_for_entity`,
  `attach_tag_to_entity`, `_save_ai_conversation_to_idea` now accept
  optional `conn=` kwarg; batch_ideas overwrite cascade calls them
  inside the manual transaction so any helper failure rolls the
  entire overwrite back together. BATCH-CREATE path intentionally
  keeps the post-commit log-and-continue helper pattern (different
  semantics — failed tag attach should not invalidate a new idea).

order: AUD-0314 (api.ts split — unblocks downstream work), then AUD-0311 +
AUD-0335 (React Query consolidation), then AUD-0309 + AUD-0319 (form layer),
then AUD-0308 + AUD-0310 + AUD-0330 (chart + journal + mega-components),
finally AUD-0337 (type tightening sweeps cleanly after structural work).

**Estimated effort:** 6-9 weeks total. **Risk:** medium-high per item.

### Wave E — Tech debt cleanup

**Items:** AUD-0030 (db_pool.py back-compat shim removal — 32 importers),

session is touching one of the affected files.
